[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:410,13] 2019-20 STATE BUDGET — LJE   143 

[2:0:189,32] 0820   Department of Justice - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The Division of Law Enforcement is organized into five elements: (1) Bureau of Firearms, (2) Bureau of Forensic Services, (3)  

[3:1:66,79] Bureau of Gambling Control, (4) Bureau of Investigation, and (5) the Office of the Chief.  

[4:0:66,99] The Bureau of Firearms provides oversight, enforcement, education, and regulation of California's firearms and  

[4:1:66,109] ammunitions   laws by conducting firearms eligibility background checks and administering over thirty different state-mandated  

[4:2:66,120] firearms-related programs. The Bureau conducts firearms dealer and manufacturer inspections for compliance, and provides  

[4:3:66,130] training as needed. Special Agents conduct investigations on armed and prohibited persons and other investigations resulting  

[4:4:66,140] in the seizure of firearms, magazines, and ammunition. Agents also conduct investigations to monitor and   prevent  

[4:5:66,150] illegal   firearm trafficking at permitted gun shows in accordance with state and federal laws.  

[5:0:66,171] The Bureau of Forensic Services (BFS) provides evaluation and analysis of physical evidence, including crime scene  

[5:1:66,181] investigation and expert court testimony to federal, state and local law enforcement agencies, district attorneys, and courts, by  

[5:2:66,191] operating 11 specialized laboratories that serve 46 counties as well as a forensic training facility. BFS maintains the state DNA  

[5:3:66,201] laboratory database which compiles DNA profiles of sex and violent offenders and felony arrestees.  

[6:0:66,222] The Bureau of Gambling Control regulates legal gambling activities in California to ensure gambling is conducted honestly and  

[6:1:66,232] is free from criminal and corruptive elements. This is accomplished by investigating the qualifications of individuals and  

[6:2:66,242] business entities who apply for state gambling licenses and monitoring the conduct of these licensees to ensure compliance  

[6:3:66,252] with the Gambling Control Act and applicable regulations. Furthermore, the Bureau conducts criminal investigations in, on or  

[6:4:66,262] about Tribal casinos and California cardrooms. The Bureau also regulates Tribal gaming to ensure that each Tribe is in  

[6:5:66,273] compliance with all aspects of the negotiated gaming compact.  

[7:0:66,293] The Bureau of Investigation is the premiere investigative agency that is responsible for exploiting and dismantling criminal  

[7:1:66,303] organizations, as well as assisting with the prosecution of serious criminal offenses which present a significant and multi-

[7:2:66,313] jurisdictional threat to California. The Bureau prioritizes investigations related to transnational criminal organizations involved in  

[7:3:66,324] gangs and human trafficking, as well as cases involving environmental crimes, public corruption, major white-collar   fraud,  

[7:4:66,334] underground economy, recycle fraud, foreign prosecution assistance agencies,   and high-technology crimes. In addition, the  

[7:5:66,344] Bureau serves a principal role in providing leadership, coordination, and support to law enforcement through multi-agency drug,  

[7:6:66,354] gang and major crimes task forces statewide.  

[8:0:66,375] The Office of the Chief enhances public safety by providing training, technical, and administrative support to the investigative,  

[8:1:66,385] regulatory and forensic components of the Division of Law Enforcement and other criminal justice agencies. The Office serves  

[8:2:66,395] as the policy-making and oversight body for its four operational bureaus.  

[9:0:66,413] 0445 - CALIFORNIA JUSTICE INFORMATION SERVICES  

[10:0:66,430] The California Justice Information Services Division provides criminal justice intelligence, information, and identification  

[10:1:66,441] services to law enforcement, regulatory agencies, and the public. Four major functional areas carry out these primary services:  

[10:2:66,451] 1) The Bureau of Criminal Identification & Investigative Services consolidates the identification, investigative, and field services  

[10:3:66,461] functions, providing information and technical assistance on manual and automated systems including the fingerprint  

[10:4:66,471] identification system and the violent crime information system; 2) The Bureau of Criminal Information and Analysis consolidates  

[10:5:66,481] the functions related to the authorization, release, and use of criminal offender record information for law enforcement  

[10:6:66,492] investigatory and regulatory purposes; 3) The Hawkins Data Center operates the Criminal Justice Information System and the  

[10:7:66,502] California Law Enforcement Telecommunications System; and 4) the Operations Support Program provides business  

[10:8:66,512] resumption planning and administrative support and oversight.  

[11:0:66,530] 9900 - DIRECTORATE AND ADMINISTRATION  

[12:0:66,547] The Directorate and the Administration Division of the Department of Justice consists of the Division of Operations and the  

[12:1:66,558] Attorney General's Executive Office. The executive office maintains overall direction and administration over the diverse  

[12:2:66,568] programs and projects of the department, including the Equal Employment Rights and Resolution Office, the Office of Program  

[12:3:66,578] Oversight and Accountability, the Opinions Unit, the Solicitor General's Unit, the Office of Legislative Affairs, the Office of  

[12:4:66,588] Communications and the Public Inquiry Unit. In addition, the Division of Operations provides support functions essential to the  

[12:5:66,598] department's operations, including fiscal, personnel, and specialized services such as legal secretarial support, litigation  

[12:6:66,609] support, and legal case management services.

[1:0:242,43] 0840   State Controller  

[2:0:66,64] The State Controller is the chief fiscal officer of California, the fifth largest economy in the world. Principally responsible for  

[2:1:66,74] transparency and accountability of the state's financial resources, the Controller ensures the appropriate disbursement and  

[2:2:66,84] tracking of taxpayer dollars. The Controller serves on dozens of state boards, commissions, and committees with  

[3:0:66,95] duties   ranging from   administrative oversight of the nation's two largest public pension funds,   to protection of state lands and  

[3:1:66,105] coastlines,   to modernization and financing of major infrastructure. The Controller also offers fiscal guidance to local  

[4:0:66,115] governments and has independent auditing authority over government agencies related to the spending of state funds. The  

[4:1:66,125] Controller's primary objectives are to:  

[5:0:65,143] • Account for and control disbursement of all state funds, issuing warrants in payment of the state's bills, including lottery  

[5:1:76,153] prizes.  

[6:0:65,169] • Determine legality and accuracy of financial claims against the state.  

[6:1:65,186] • Audit state and local government programs.  

[7:0:65,202] • Safeguard many types of assets until claimed by the rightful owners, in accordance with the Unclaimed Property Law.  

[7:1:65,218] • Inform the public of the state's financial condition.  

[8:0:65,234] • Inform the public of financial transactions of city, county, and other local governments.  

[8:1:65,250] • Administer the Uniform State Payroll System.  

[9:0:65,267] • Audit and process all personnel and payroll transactions for state civil service, state exempt employees, state university  

[9:1:76,277] employees, and college system employees.

[10:0:66,584] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[10:1:66,602] 0500100 - ACCOUNTING AND REPORTING  

[11:0:66,623] The State Accounting and Reporting Division maintains uniform and systematic control accounts of all receipts, payments,  

[11:1:66,633] state fund balances, and bonded indebtedness; reports the financial condition of the state; monitors the cash flow of the  

[11:2:66,643] General Fund; administers the statewide discharge from accountability program; participates in offsetting monies owed to the  

[11:3:66,653] state; and collaborates with the Department of Finance, the Treasurer, and the Department of General Services to develop and  

[11:4:66,664] implement the Financial Information System for California (FI$Cal) to ensure the system meets the state's primary objectives  

[11:5:66,674] and provides best business practices for the state.  

[12:0:66,694] The Local Government Programs and Services Division maintains a database of information and reports on local financial  

[12:1:66,704] transactions and government compensation; apportions shared revenues to local governments; administers local mandated  

[12:2:66,715] cost programs; approves county cost allocation plans; prescribes uniform accounting procedures for presentation of financial

[3:4:66,117] 0500200 - AUDITS  

[4:0:66,137] The Audits Division determines the legality and accuracy of all claims against the state through the performance of prepayment  

[4:1:66,148] audits; assures the accuracy of local government claims and financial statements submitted to the state and federal  

[4:2:66,158] governments by establishing and updating audit guidelines, and reviewing audits performed by independent auditors; performs  

[4:3:66,168] field audits for state and federal programs; reviews the single audit reports of local governments and local education agencies

[4:5:66,188] Property Law.  

[5:0:66,206] 0500300 - PERSONNEL/PAYROLL SERVICES  

[6:0:66,226] The Personnel/Payroll Services Division administers the state's payroll, employment history, the automated travel expense  

[6:1:66,237] reimbursement system, and leave accounting processes in a manner that provides accurate, timely, and efficient processing for  

[6:2:66,247] the users of these systems. The Division works with   the Department of Human Resources, California Public Employees'  

[6:3:66,257] Retirement System, Judicial Council, Department of Finance, and California State University Chancellor's Office to maximize  

[6:4:66,267] the efficiency of the state's personnel and payroll functions.  

[7:0:66,288] The California State Payroll System Project was initiated to modernize the statewide human resource management and  

[7:1:66,298] payroll   systems as part of a fully integrated solution. Both modernizing the existing system as well as replacement of the  

[7:2:66,308] existing system will be evaluated as solutions. The system should enable the state to improve management processes and  

[7:3:66,318] fulfill its payroll, reporting, and deduction processing obligations accurately and on time.  

[7:4:66,336] 0500400 - UNCLAIMED PROPERTY  

[8:0:66,356] The Unclaimed Property Division administers the Unclaimed Property Law by providing one central source for owners to claim  

[8:1:66,367] their property; notifying owners of their unclaimed property before it is transferred to the state; receiving unclaimed property  

[8:2:66,377] from banks, savings and loans, insurance companies,   and other business firms; and providing outreach and education for  

[8:3:66,387] businesses holding unclaimed property.  

[8:4:66,405] 0500500 - DISBURSEMENTS  

[9:0:66,425] The Disbursements Bureau produces and delivers all payments of the state's obligations after auditing and clearance through  

[9:1:66,435] control accounts, including personal income tax refunds, payroll, vendor,   and retirement payments. Disbursements also  

[9:2:66,445] provides post-issuance services including disposition of undeliverable warrants; lost warrant duplication; and maintenance and  

[9:3:66,456] production of paid warrant images.  

[9:4:66,473] 0500900 - DEPARTMENTAL ADMINISTRATION  

[10:0:66,494] The Executive Office and the Administration Program provide executive direction and support services to all   Divisions in the  

[10:1:66,504] State Controller's Office. The Information Systems Division develops, maintains, and operates all of the department's  

[10:2:66,514] mainframe, client-server and web-based systems; and oversees the planning, procurement, use, and maintenance of  

[10:3:66,524] information technology hardware and software.

[0:0:66,13] 2019-20 STATE BUDGET — LJE   180   LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:216,43] 0845   Department of Insurance  

[2:0:66,64] California's publicly-elected Insurance Commissioner regulates the fourth largest insurance economy in the world with insurers  

[2:1:66,74] collecting more than $310 billion in premiums annually in California while protecting consumers and the integrity, health and  

[2:2:66,84] vitality of the insurance marketplace. The vision of the California Department of Insurance (CDI) is "Insurance Protection for All  

[2:3:66,95] Californians." CDI accomplishes this by enforcing insurance laws and regulations, assisting consumers in their dealings with  

[2:4:66,105] insurers, and using innovation to improve services for insurance producers and consumers.  

[3:0:66,123] The CDI licenses and regulates insurance companies, and individuals in California. Currently, the CDI oversees and licenses  

[3:1:66,133] approximately 1,400 insurance companies and approximately 410,000 individuals and business entities as insurance agents,  

[3:2:66,143] brokers, adjusters and bail agents. Additionally, the CDI receives and investigates approximately 200,000 consumer inquiries  

[3:3:66,153] and complaints annually; performs examinations to ensure the financial solvency of companies; receives more than 28,000  

[3:4:66,163] suspected fraudulent claim referrals annually; receives and reviews approximately 7,250 rate filing applications annually; and  

[3:5:66,174] works in conjunction with local, state and federal law enforcement agencies to investigate and prosecute fraudulent insurance  

[3:6:66,184] practices.

[7:0:66,365] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[8:0:66,384] 0520 - REGULATION OF INSURANCE COMPANIES AND INSURANCE PRODUCERS  

[9:0:66,401] The objectives of this program are to: (1) prevent losses to policyholders, beneficiaries or the public due to the insolvency of  

[9:1:66,412] insurers, including the review of complex, principles-based reserving methods to avoid reliance on black box models; (2)  

[9:2:66,422] prevent unlawful or unfair practices by insurers as defined by the Insurance Code; (3) ensure that property and casualty  

[9:3:66,432] insurance rates are not excessive, inadequate, unfairly discriminatory or otherwise in violation of the Insurance Code and the  

[9:4:66,442] California Code of Regulations; (4) review health insurance rates filed with CDI to determine whether they are reasonable and  

[9:5:66,452] attempt to get unreasonable rates lowered by insurers; and (5) ensure that applicants for insurance licenses, and holders of  

[9:6:66,463] insurance licenses, satisfy and maintain the qualifications for licensure. Through the Conservation and Liquidation Office, the  

[9:7:66,473] CDI administers the estates of insolvent and delinquent insurance companies.  

[9:8:66,490] 0525 - CONSUMER PROTECTION  

[10:0:66,508] The objectives of this program are to: (1) provide direct service to California consumers by protecting insurance policyholders  

[10:1:66,518] and other parties involved in insurance transactions against unfair or illegal practices with respect to claims handling, rating or  

[10:2:66,529] underwriting by insurers and (2) protect applicants and policyholders from discriminatory, unlawful or fraudulent practices or  

[10:3:66,539] incompetence relating to the sale of insurance and (3) oversee programs that benefit California's underserved communities.  

[10:4:66,556] 0530 - FRAUD CONTROL  

[11:0:66,574] The objective of this program is to protect the public from economic loss by actively investigating, arresting and referring for  

[11:1:66,584] prosecution or adjudication those who commit insurance fraud and other violations of the law. The program is primarily staffed  

[11:2:66,595] by sworn peace officers who conduct criminal investigations of insurance fraud and related criminal cases. The program also  

[11:3:66,605] implements the Insurance Frauds Prevention Act, which authorizes the Commissioner to initiate or intervene in whistle-blower  

[11:4:66,615] "qui tam" actions seeking civil penalties against perpetrators of insurance fraud.  

[11:5:66,633] 0535 - GENERAL FUND TAX COLLECTION AND COMPLIANCE  

[12:0:66,650] This program performs tax collection; ensures compliance from insurance companies and surplus line brokers with the laws  

[12:1:66,661] contained in the Insurance Code and Revenue and Taxation Code; and works with California Department of Tax and Fee  

[12:2:66,671] Administration and State Controller's Office with various refund, assessment, and accounting matters relative to the premium  

[12:3:66,681] tax program. Tax collections from this program are deposited in the state's General Fund.  

[13:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[0:0:66,13] 2019-20 STATE BUDGET — LJE   188   LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[1:0:183,43] 0850   California State Lottery Commission  

[2:0:66,64] In 1984, Proposition 37 amended the California Constitution to authorize the establishment of a statewide lottery. As an  

[2:1:66,74] initiative statute, the California State Lottery Act (Act) of 1984 created the California State Lottery Commission and gave it  

[2:2:66,84] broad powers to oversee the operations of a statewide lottery. The purpose of the Act was to provide supplemental monies to  

[2:3:66,95] benefit public education. The Lottery is overseen by a five-person Commission appointed by the Governor and confirmed by  

[2:4:66,105] the State Senate.  

[3:0:66,125] The Act initially required that 50 percent of total annual revenues be returned to the public in the form of prizes and at least 34  

[3:1:66,135] percent of total revenues be allocated to the benefit of public education. No more than 16 percent of total revenues were to be  

[3:2:66,146] used for administrative costs.  

[4:0:66,166] In 2010, the Act was changed to allow the Lottery flexibility to pay out more money in prizes and reduce the administrative cost  

[4:1:66,176] limit to 13 percent of total revenues. Along with that flexibility, the new law requires the Lottery to meet minimum levels of  

[4:2:66,186] contribution to public education. Revenues to education are placed in a special fund, known as the California State Lottery  

[4:3:66,197] Education Fund, which holds revenues until they are allocated on a per capita basis, using prior year certified Average Daily  

[4:4:66,207] Attendance data, to the following categories: K-12 education, Community Colleges, the California State University, the  

[4:5:66,217] University of California, and other educational entities, including the California Schools for the Deaf and Blind.  

[5:0:66,237] In the 33 years since sales began in October 1985 through June 30, 2018, the California State Lottery has raised $34.2 billion  

[5:1:66,248] for public education, including $1.7 billion in FY 2017-18.  

[6:0:66,268] Because of the inherently variable nature of lottery ticket sales, revenue estimates for 2018-19 and 2019-20 cannot be made  

[6:1:66,278] with certainty.  

[7:0:66,305] LEGAL CITATIONS AND AUTHORITY  

[8:0:66,323] DEPARTMENT AUTHORITY  

[9:0:66,344] Government Code, Title 2, Division 1, Chapter 12.5 (Sections 8880-8880.72).

[1:0:169,43] 0855   California Gambling Control Commission  

[2:0:66,64] The mission of the California Gambling Control Commission (Commission) is to ensure integrity in California's gaming  

[2:1:66,74] environment. The Commission has jurisdiction over gambling establishments (cardrooms), third-party providers of proposition  

[2:2:66,84] player services, and certain aspects of Tribal casinos, pursuant to its authority under state law and Tribal-State Gaming  

[2:3:66,95] Compacts (Compacts). The Commission also has jurisdiction over gaming policies, regulations, criteria, and standards.  

[3:0:66,115] There are 89 licensed cardrooms in California over which the Commission has broad regulatory and adjudicatory authority. This  

[3:1:66,125] authority extends to the operation, concentration, and supervision of the cardrooms and all persons and things related to each  

[3:2:66,135] licensed establishment.  

[4:0:66,156] The Commission has fiduciary, regulatory, and administrative responsibilities related to Tribal gaming that include: (1)  

[4:1:66,166] distributing specified Tribal gaming revenues to Non-Compact, Non-Gaming and Limited-Gaming Tribes; (2) making suitability  

[4:2:66,176] determinations for key employees, gaming resource suppliers, and financial sources; and (3) serving as the administrator of the  

[4:3:66,186] Indian Gaming Revenue Sharing Trust Fund, Indian Gaming Special Distribution Fund, and the Tribal Nation Grant Fund.

[1:0:209,43] 0860   State Board of Equalization  

[1:1:66,64] The State Board of Equalization's (BOE)   duties   primarily include assessing and allocating the property values of railroads and  

[1:2:66,74] specified utilities and businesses; adjudicating property tax appeals of taxable government owned property; overseeing the  

[1:3:66,84] property tax assessment practices of the 58 county assessors; adopting rules to clarify property tax laws; and administering the  

[1:4:66,95] alcoholic beverage excise tax and the insurance tax, including appeals. The BOE contracts with the   California Department of  

[1:5:66,105] Tax and Fee Administration (CDTFA)   to administer the alcoholic beverage tax and insurance tax program.

[6:0:66,296] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,314] 0570025 - COUNTY ASSESSMENT STANDARDS PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,332] This program ensures that taxable properties are enrolled and assessed by the 58 county assessors in full conformity with the  

[7:1:66,342] law. The BOE is also charged with providing consultation and services to the county assessors and their staff, establishing  

[7:2:66,352] standards, providing training for assessors and assessment appeals boards, evaluating the effectiveness of each county  

[7:3:66,362] assessor's administration, co-administering the welfare exemption, and administering the Legal Entity Ownership Program.  

[7:4:66,380] 0570050 - STATE-ASSESSED PROPERTY PROGRAM  

[8:0:66,401] This program   values and assesses   inter-county pipelines and properties owned or used by railroads, regulated telephone  

[8:1:66,411] companies, companies transmitting or selling gas or electricity, and private railroad car companies. Local jurisdictions use the  

[8:2:66,421] established values for the levy and collection of local property taxes. In addition, the BOE collects the Private Railroad Car Tax  

[8:3:66,431] that is deposited in the state General Fund.  

[8:4:66,449] 0570150 - ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGE TAX PROGRAM  

[9:0:66,469] This program collects the excise tax imposed on the sale, distribution, or importation of alcoholic beverages in California. The  

[9:1:66,479] BOE contracts with the CDTFA to administer this program.  

[9:2:66,497] 0570575 - INSURANCE TAX PROGRAM  

[10:0:66,518] This program provides revenue to the Insurance Tax Fund. Revenue is generated from taxes assessed on insurance  

[10:1:66,528] premiums, underwriting profits from ocean marine insurance, and retaliatory assessments levied on   out-of-state insurers. The  

[10:2:66,538] taxes collected are used to pay refunds or transferred to the General Fund. The BOE contracts with the CDTFA to administer  

[10:3:66,548] this program.

[1:0:226,43] 0870   Office of Tax Appeals  

[2:0:66,64] The Office of Tax Appeals (OTA) was established effective January 1, 2018, by Chapter 16, Statutes of 2017 (AB 102). The  

[2:1:66,74] OTA performs those tax appeal duties formerly assigned by statute to the State Board of Equalization, including personal  

[2:2:66,84] income tax appeals, franchise tax appeals, and sales and use tax appeals. The OTA's mission is to ensure tax appeals are  

[2:3:66,95] performed in a fair, transparent, consistent, equitable, and impartial manner.  

[3:0:66,115] The OTA has hearing offices in Sacramento, Fresno, and Los Angeles.

[3:0:66,88] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,106] 0620100 - EXECUTIVE DIVISION  

[4:0:66,124] The Executive Division provides leadership and direction to the OTA, and empowers staff to perform their duties fairly,  

[4:1:66,134] impartially, and in strict conformance with applicable statutes and regulations.  

[4:2:66,152] 0620200 - ADMINISTRATION DIVISION  

[5:0:66,172] The Administration Division ensures the efficient operation of the OTA by providing fiscal oversight and performing personnel  

[5:1:66,182] management, information technology, and business services functions.  

[5:2:66,200] 0620300 - HEARINGS DIVISION  

[6:0:66,220] The Hearings Division is responsible for hearing and determining tax appeals arising from taxpayer disputes from assessments  

[6:1:66,231] made by the Franchise Tax Board and the Department of Tax and Fee Administration.   It is   responsible for writing and  

[6:2:66,241] publishing decisions for each case that comes before OTA.  

[6:3:66,259] 0620400 - FOUNDATIONS   DIVISION  

[7:0:66,276] The   Foundations Division is responsible for preparing and developing cases for Administrative Law Judge (ALJ) determination.  

[7:1:66,286] They are subject matter experts in tax law who use their expertise to expedite the ALJ determination process.

[1:0:236,43] 0890   Secretary of State  

[2:0:66,64] The Secretary of State, a constitutionally established office, is the chief elections officer of the state and is responsible for the  

[2:1:66,74] administration and enforcement of election laws. The Office also is responsible for administering and enforcing laws pertaining  

[2:2:66,84] to filing documents associated with corporations, limited liability companies, partnerships, limited partnerships, unincorporated  

[2:3:66,95] associations and pertaining to filing bonds and perfecting security agreements. In addition, the Office is responsible for  

[2:4:66,105] commissioning notaries public, enforcing the notary laws, and in conjunction with being the home of the State Archives,  

[3:0:66,115] administering a state records management program and preserving documents and records having historical significance. The  

[3:1:66,125] Secretary of State is the filing officer for lobbying and campaign registration and disclosure documents filed under the Political  

[3:2:66,135] Reform Act. The Secretary of State also operates the Safe at Home program, maintains the Domestic Partners and Advance  

[3:3:66,146] Health Care Directives registries, provides support functions for the Voting Modernization Board, and is home to the California  

[3:4:66,156] Museum.  

[4:0:66,176] Policy associated with the administration of the Office is accomplished through the divisions of Elections, Political Reform,  

[4:1:66,186] Business Programs, Archives, Information Technology, and Management Services.

[5:0:66,255] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,274] 0700 - FILINGS AND REGISTRATIONS  

[7:0:66,294] The Business Programs Division is comprised of three primary areas: Business Entities, Uniform Commercial Code, and  

[7:1:66,304] Notary Public and Special Filings.  

[8:0:66,325] Business Entities examines, files, and maintains formation documents for new California business entities and qualifies out-of-

[8:1:66,335] state and international entities to conduct business in California; and also examines, files and maintains changes to the records  

[8:2:66,345] of domestic or qualified foreign business entities to ensure the business entities are properly formed, merged, converted,  

[8:3:66,355] amended, and dissolved in compliance with California law. Statements of Information containing key officers and contact  

[8:4:66,365] information are also processed and maintained for public and governmental use.  

[9:0:66,386] Uniform Commercial Code files certain financing statements allowing lending institutions to protect their financial interest in  

[9:1:66,396] personal property and established priority in case of debtor default or bankruptcy. Notices of judgment liens, attachment liens,  

[9:2:66,406] agricultural liens, and equipment liens are also filed in Uniform Commercial Code, as well as notices of various tax liens  

[9:3:66,416] submitted by state and federal taxing agencies such as the Franchise Tax Board and the Internal Revenue Service.  

[10:0:66,437] Notary Public and Special Filings appoints and commissions qualified notaries public for four- year terms, reviews and  

[10:1:66,447] approves notary public education courses, and certifies to the authenticity of signatures of notaries public and public officials on  

[10:2:66,457] documents for use in foreign countries. Special Filings include trademarks and service marks as well as surety bonds that  

[10:3:66,467] certain business entities are required to file, notices of joint power agreements, city and county charters, and claims for  

[10:4:66,478] successor-in-interest. This area also has disciplinary functions with regard to notaries public and immigration consultants.  

[11:0:66,498] The Advance Health Care Directive (AHCD) Registry maintains AHCDs, which allow a person to indicate his/her medical  

[11:1:66,508] treatment preferences if he/she cannot speak or make decisions for him/herself. The AHCD also may designate someone else  

[11:2:66,518] to make decisions regarding medical treatment. AHCDs and related information can be provided upon request to the  

[11:3:66,529] registrant's health care provider, public guardian, or legal representative.  

[12:0:66,549] The Domestic Partners Registry registers same-sex couples regardless of the age of the partners, and opposite-sex couples in  

[12:1:66,559] which one partner is at least 62 years old, as domestic partners in California.  

[13:0:66,580] The Victims of Corporate Fraud Compensation Fund provides limited restitution to victims of corporate fraud who are unable to  

[13:1:66,590] collect through other means on a judgment against a corporation for corporate fraud.  

[14:0:66,610] Safe at Home is a confidential mail forwarding program designed to assist victims of domestic violence and human trafficking,  

[14:1:66,620] sexual assault, stalking, or a reproductive healthcare employee, patient, or volunteer. Participants in the Safe at Home program  

[14:2:66,631] are provided with a free post office box to use as a substitute mailing address, thereby protecting their actual residential  

[14:3:66,641] address. Once enrolled into the program, Safe at Home serves as a liaison for those participants who qualify for additional  

[14:4:66,651] confidential services offered by various state and local agencies.  

[15:0:66,669] 0705 - ELECTIONS  

[16:0:66,686] The Secretary of State, as California's chief elections officer, has broad responsibility to administer the election process. This  

[16:1:66,697] program oversees all federal and state elections within California, maintaining a statewide database of all registered voters,  

[16:2:66,707] tracks and certifies ballot measures, certifies candidates, and certifies election results. In addition, the program oversees the  

[17:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,69] modernization of voting equipment and the improvement of current electoral database systems, enhancing the voting  

[3:1:66,79] processes, providing accessibility to voters, working to increase people's knowledge of the electoral system, and investigates  

[3:2:66,89] election related criminal violations as provided by California Elections Code.  

[4:0:66,107] This program includes the campaign and lobbying registration and disclosure provisions of the Political Reform Act of 1974.  

[4:1:66,117] Under this law, the Office registers all levels of campaign committees, and reviews for compliance with statutory requirements  

[4:2:66,127] all state-level candidate and campaign recipient committees, major donors, slate mailer, political party, and independent  

[4:3:66,137] expenditure committees. The program registers lobbyists (including placement agents), lobbying firms and lobbyist employers,  

[4:4:66,148] reviews for compliance with statutory requirements the periodic financial disclosure reports filed by lobbying entities, and  

[4:5:66,158] publishes a Lobbying Directory on the Internet. This program also supports the electronic filing requirements of the Political  

[4:6:66,168] Reform Act and posts relevant registration and disclosure information to the Office's web site so the public can track where  

[4:7:66,178] campaign money is raised and spent and what lobbying activity is occurring in state government. A searchable database of  

[4:8:66,188] campaign and lobbying financial activity is also provided through the web site.  

[4:9:66,206] 0710 - ARCHIVES  

[5:0:66,224] The California State Archives establishes and administers a records management program that applies efficient and  

[5:1:66,234] economical management methods to the creation, utilization, maintenance, retention, preservation, and disposal of state  

[5:2:66,244] records and acquires, indexes, preserves, and provides reference access to irreplaceable historic materials from the three  

[5:3:66,254] branches of state government. The Archives acquires physical and electronic records with legal, administrative or evidentiary  

[5:4:66,265] value, or that have historical significance. Materials are transferred to the Archives for permanent preservation.  

[5:5:66,282] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION  

[6:0:66,300] This program develops and manages overall policy. It serves as the liaison to other state agencies, the Legislature, the federal  

[6:1:66,310] government, and other states' Secretaries of State. This program responds to constituent correspondence and requests from  

[6:2:66,320] the public and advocates in the Legislature, administers the Secretary's role as a member of the National Association of  

[6:3:66,331] Secretaries of State, in the management of task forces and advisory committees, in the implementation of new federal and  

[6:4:66,341] state statutory requirements, and coordinates and disseminates information about the Office and its initiatives to the public. It  

[6:5:66,351] also provides the Office with the necessary personnel, general administrative, budgeting, fiscal services, and information  

[6:6:66,361] technology expertise to plan, develop, implement, and operate innovative and effective business and information systems  

[6:7:66,371] solutions.

[1:0:243,43] 0950   State Treasurer  

[2:0:66,64] The State Treasurer, a constitutionally established office, provides banking services for state government with goals to  

[2:1:66,74] minimize interest and service costs and to maximize yield on investments. The Treasurer is responsible for the custody of all  

[2:2:66,84] monies and securities belonging to or held in trust by the state; investment of temporarily idle state monies; administration of  

[2:3:66,95] the sale of state bonds, their redemption and interest payments; and payment of warrants or checks drawn by the State  

[2:4:66,105] Controller and other state agencies.

[5:0:66,140] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,159] 0740010 - INVESTMENT SERVICES  

[7:0:66,179] The Investment Division is responsible for investment of state monies from the date of receipt through the date of redemption.  

[7:1:66,189] During the 2017-18 fiscal year, this Division handled 8,573 security investment transactions totaling $392 billion. The Pooled  

[7:2:66,199] Money Investment Board (PMIB) program accounted for 6,945 of these transactions totaling $346 billion; time deposits  

[7:3:66,210] accounted for 1,256 transactions totaling $32.2 billion. The remaining $13.8 billion is invested on behalf of the state's special  

[7:4:66,220] funds, such as those associated with the California Housing Finance Agency, the Department of Fish and Wildlife, the state's  

[7:5:66,230] retirement system, etc. The Division also administers the Local Agency Investment Fund (LAIF), a voluntary investment  

[7:6:66,240] program created to offer California local agencies greater access to the financial markets through the PMIB program. In the  

[7:7:66,250] 2017-18 fiscal year, 2,438 local agencies participated in LAIF, with deposits averaging $21.4 billion for the fiscal year.  

[8:0:66,268] 0740019 - CENTRALIZED TREASURY AND SECURITIES MANAGEMENT  

[9:0:66,286] In 1949, the California Legislature amended Government Code Section 16305 to create the Centralized Treasury System  

[9:1:66,296] (CTS) thereby requiring agencies of the State to deposit their money in trust with the Treasurer. The legislation also requires  

[9:2:66,306] the Treasurer to safeguard the money and make safe and prudent investments. In 1955, the Legislature created the PMIB,  

[9:3:66,316] giving the Board the responsibility to designate the amount of money available for the investment in securities, bank deposits,  

[9:4:66,327] and loans to the General Fund.  

[10:0:66,344] The Centralized Treasury and Securities Management Division (CTSMD) oversees all banking aspects of the CTS. The goal of  

[10:1:66,355] the CTSMD is to maximize the earning of interest consistent with safe and prudent treasury management, and to ensure that  

[10:2:66,365] the depository banks provide the state with proper and adequate security for the deposit of state monies. The Treasurer  

[10:3:66,375] maintains demand bank accounts with eight banks for the purpose of providing necessary statewide depository coverage for  

[10:4:66,385] the remittance of funds collected by the various state agencies.  

[11:0:66,403] The CTSMD 1) monitors the cash flow of all state funds, forecasts cash balances, revenue, expenditures, and the amounts  

[11:1:66,413] available for daily investments, 2) ensures accurate and timely agency deposits, 3) administers and executes the wire transfer  

[11:2:66,423] of funds, 4) reconciles state accounts with depository banks and redeems all state items submitted by presenting banks for  

[11:3:66,433] payments, 5) executes the clearance and income collection for state investments (excluding PERS and STRS) and securities  

[11:4:66,444] pledged to the state, 6) fulfills the clearance and settlement of securities pledged to the state for the time, demand, and other  

[11:5:66,454] state agency programs, and 7) is responsible for the safekeeping of securities and other personal property owned by or  

[11:6:66,464] pledged to the state.  

[12:0:66,482] 0740028 - PUBLIC FINANCE  

[13:0:66,499] The Public Finance Division is responsible for selling State of California general obligation bonds, commercial paper notes,  

[13:1:66,510] revenue anticipation notes, lease revenue bonds, revenue bonds, and any other indebtedness for all state agencies. The  

[13:2:66,520] Division provides debt administration services for most state bonds and is responsible for disseminating information to  

[13:3:66,530] bondholders through the Investor Relations Program.  

[14:0:66,548] The Division also assures compliance with federal tax laws applicable to state debt so there is no adverse consequences to  

[14:1:66,558] bondholders or increased borrowing costs to the state. The post-issuance tax compliance for various state debt includes  

[14:2:66,568] monitoring the use of bond proceeds, managing rebate and yield restriction compliance, coordinating necessary financial  

[14:3:66,578] disclosure, and ensuring proper record keeping.  

[15:0:66,596] 0740035 - ADMINISTRATION AND INFORMATION SERVICES  

[16:0:66,614] The Administration Division, Executive Office, and the Information Services Division provide executive direction and support  

[16:1:66,624] services to programs in the State Treasurer's Office. Services include budgeting, personnel, accounting, information systems,  

[16:2:66,634] business services, technical support, and production operations.  

[17:0:66,675] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM

[5:0:66,154] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,172] 0780 - GOLDEN STATE SCHOLARSHARE COLLEGE SAVINGS TRUST PROGRAM  

[5:2:66,190] The Golden State ScholarShare College Savings Trust Program is California's state-sponsored 529 college savings plan  

[5:3:66,200] established to help families save for higher education.   Earnings are tax-free when used for qualified higher education expenses  

[5:4:66,210] (such as tuition, fees, supplies, books, computer equipment, and certain room and board expenses) at eligible educational  

[5:5:66,220] institutions.  

[5:6:66,238] 0785 - GOVERNOR'S SCHOLARSHIP PROGRAMS  

[6:0:66,256] The Governor's Scholarship Programs (GSP) rewarded public school students who demonstrated high academic achievement  

[6:1:66,266] with scholarships.   Students may have earned multiple $1,000 Governor's Scholars Awards and a one-time $2,500 Governor's  

[6:2:66,276] Distinguished Mathematics and Science Scholars Award for scores attained on tests taken in 2000, 2001, and 2002. GSP  

[6:3:66,286] became inoperative and was repealed after 2002.   The ScholarShare Investment Board administers scholarship awards that  

[6:4:66,297] were already earned.  

[6:5:66,314] 0790 - CALIFORNIA MEMORIAL SCHOLARSHIP PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,332] The California Memorial Scholarship Program provides scholarships to surviving dependents of California residents killed as a  

[7:1:66,342] result of the terrorist attacks of September 11, 2001.

[1:0:134,43] 0956   California Debt and Investment Advisory Commission

[1:2:66,74] finance in California by providing responsive and reliable information, analysis, and training. The Commission assists California  

[1:3:66,84] state and local governments to monitor, issue, and manage public debt and to safely and prudently invest public funds.  

[2:0:66,105] The Commission consists of nine members including the State Treasurer, who serves as chairperson; the Governor or, upon

[1:0:165,43] 0959   California Debt Limit Allocation Committee  

[2:0:66,64] The California Debt Limit Allocation Committee's mission is to allocate tax-exempt, private activity bond authority for the State  

[2:1:66,74] of California. Private activity bonds may be used by the private sector for projects and programs that provide a public benefit,  

[2:2:66,84] such as the creation of affordable housing.  

[3:0:66,105] The federal government limits the total amount of tax-exempt private activity bond authority that can be issued on an annual  

[3:1:66,115] basis. Except for the Qualified Public Educational Facility Bond Program, the bond authority limit (debt limit) is calculated by  

[3:2:66,125] multiplying the state population by $105. California's limit totaled over $4.1 billion in 2018. (California's limit for the Qualified  

[3:3:66,135] Public Educational Facility Bond Program is calculated separately by multiplying the state population by $10, and totaled $395  

[3:4:66,146] million for 2018.)  

[4:0:66,166] The Committee's allocation of tax-exempt bond authority results in the issuance of bonds by cities, counties, joint powers  

[4:1:66,176] authorities and state agencies. The bonds are purchased and used by the private sector and are not an obligation of the state  

[4:2:66,186] or federal government.  

[5:0:66,207] The Committee administers   six active programs that are funded through the allocation and issuance of tax-exempt private  

[5:1:66,217] activity bonds.   The Committee is funded on a fee-supported basis and is comprised of the State Treasurer (Chairperson), the  

[5:2:66,227] Governor, or upon his designation, the Director of Finance, and the State Controller.

[15:1:66,712] support below-market interest rate mortgage loans; and mortgage credit certificates (MCCs) that reduce a homebuyer's federal

[2:0:130,32] 0959   California Debt Limit Allocation Committee - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] tax liability. Below is a summary of each program:  

[4:0:66,89] Qualified Residential Rental Project Program - Tax-exempt housing revenue bonds lower the cost for developers of multifamily  

[4:1:66,99] rental housing to acquire land and construct new housing or purchase and rehabilitate existing housing. The developers  

[4:2:66,109] produce affordable rental housing for low-income households by reducing rental rates charged to these individuals and  

[4:3:66,120] families. Projects that receive an award of bond authority can apply for non-competitive four-percent tax credits using the  

[4:4:66,130] California Debt Limit Allocation Committee/California Tax Credit Allocation Committee Joint Application.  

[5:0:66,150] Single-Family Housing Program - Tax-exempt MRBs or MCCs to assist first-time homebuyers with purchasing homes.  

[5:1:66,160] Homebuyers may purchase single-family homes, either freestanding or detached, condominiums, or townhouses. Program  

[5:2:66,171] participants must meet income limits and must purchase a home that falls within the program's purchase price limitations.  

[6:0:66,191] Home Improvement and Rehabilitation Bond Program - MRBs or MCCs to assist homeowners with home improvement  

[6:1:66,201] financing. Homeowners may improve single-family homes, either freestanding or detached, condominiums, or townhouses.  

[6:2:66,211] Program participants must meet income limits, and in certain cases, must own a home that falls within the program's  

[6:3:66,222] rehabilitation cost and age-of-home limitations.  

[7:0:66,242] Industrial Development Bond Project Program - Small-Issue industrial development bonds are tax-exempt private activity bonds  

[7:1:66,252] issued to assist manufacturing facilities finance capital expenditures. These bonds offer interest rate savings to small and  

[7:2:66,262] midsize manufacturers in contrast to conventional loans, and help manufacturers retain and create new jobs within their  

[7:3:66,273] communities.  

[8:0:66,293] Exempt Facility Program - Tax-exempt private activity bonds issued to finance solid waste disposal and waste recycling  

[8:1:66,303] facilities. Loan interest rate savings enable the project owners to charge lower customer rates, while assisting communities  

[8:2:66,313] they serve to meet mandated requirements to protect and enhance the environment.  

[9:0:66,334] Qualified Public Educational Facility Bond Program - Tax-exempt private activity bonds issued to finance the construction,  

[9:1:66,344] renovation, and furnishing of primary and secondary school facilities.

[1:0:157,43] 0964   California Transportation Financing Authority  

[1:1:66,64] The California Transportation Financing Authority was established by Chapter 474, Statutes of 2009, to increase the  

[1:2:66,74] construction of new capacity or improvements for the state transportation system in a manner that will help achieve the state's  

[1:3:66,84] goals of reducing greenhouse gas, improving air quality, and conserving natural resources.  

[2:0:66,105] The Authority consists of seven members: the State Treasurer (Chairperson), the Director of the Department of Finance, the  

[2:1:66,115] State Controller, the Director of Transportation, the Executive Director of the California Transportation Commission, a local  

[2:2:66,125] agency representative appointed by the Senate Committee on Rules, and a local agency representative appointed by the  

[2:3:66,135] Speaker of the Assembly.

[10:0:66,398] 0820 - CALIFORNIA TRANSPORTATION FINANCING AUTHORITY  

[11:0:66,418] The Authority was established to assist transportation agencies in obtaining financing to develop transportation projects. To  

[11:1:66,428] meet this objective, statutes allow the Authority to issue, or to approve specified project sponsors to issue revenue bonds to  

[11:2:66,438] fund transportation projects backed in whole or in part, by various revenue streams of transportation funds (including toll  

[11:3:66,449] revenues). Statutes provide the authority to approve the imposition and collection of tolls on proposed transportation projects  

[11:4:66,459] under certain conditions. The planning, programming, and allocation of transportation projects are performed by the California  

[11:5:66,469] Transportation Commission and the California Department of Transportation, as appropriate.

[1:0:96,43] 0965   California Industrial Development Financing Advisory Commission  

[1:1:66,64] The California Industrial Development Financing Advisory Commission creates employment opportunities and supports local  

[1:2:66,74] economic development by approving local entities' issuance of industrial development bonds. These bonds provide  

[1:3:66,84] manufacturers with a low-cost financing option to build, expand, or equip their facilities in California. The Commission  

[1:4:66,95] independently reviews bond applications to ensure compliance with federal tax law and state law, provides technical assistance  

[1:5:66,105] to bond issuers, and approves the bond sales by local authorities.  

[2:0:66,125] The State Treasurer serves as chairperson of the Commission. The other members are the Director of the Department of  

[2:1:66,135] Finance, the State Controller, the Director of the Governor's Office of Business and Economic Development, and the  

[2:2:66,146] Commissioner of the Department of Business Oversight.

[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE   2019-20 STATE BUDGET — LJE   235 

[1:0:166,43] 0968   California Tax Credit Allocation Committee  

[2:0:66,64] The mission of the California Tax Credit Allocation Committee is to fairly allocate federal and state tax credits to create and  

[2:1:66,74] maintain safe, quality affordable rental housing for low-income households in California. The Committee does this by forming  

[2:2:66,84] partnerships with developers, investors and public entities.  

[3:0:66,105] The Committee assists development of rental housing projects for low-income families and monitors these projects for years  

[3:1:66,115] after they are placed in service to ensure compliance with income and rent restrictions related to the tax credit programs of the  

[3:2:66,125] Committee. Coordinating with state and local housing fund providers, and with private investors, the Committee helps to create  

[3:3:66,135] and maintain a supply of quality, affordable housing.  

[4:0:66,156] The Committee consists of seven members, including three voting members and four advisors. The voting members are the  

[4:1:66,166] Treasurer (Chairperson of the Committee), the Governor (who may choose the Director of Finance as his or her  

[4:2:66,176] representative), and the State Controller. The non-voting (advisory) members are the Director of Housing and Community  

[4:3:66,186] Development, the Executive Director of the California Housing Finance Agency, and two local government representatives.  

[4:4:66,197] One local representative is associated with a city government and appointed by the Speaker of the Assembly. The other is a  

[4:5:66,207] county government representative appointed by the Senate Rules Committee.

[5:0:66,243] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,261] 0840 - CALIFORNIA TAX CREDIT ALLOCATION COMMITTEE  

[6:0:66,281] The Federal Program  

[7:0:66,302] Congress authorized the federal Low-Income Housing Tax Credit (LIHTC) program in 1986. It replaced traditional housing tax  

[7:1:66,312] incentives, such as accelerated depreciation, with a tax credit that enables developers of affordable rental housing to raise  

[7:2:66,322] project equity through the "sale" of tax benefits to investors. The federal per-capita tax credit ceiling is calculated annually and  

[7:3:66,332] indexed for inflation. 

[8:0:66,353] Two types of federal tax credits are available, generally referred to as 9-percent and 4-percent credits. These terms refer to the  

[8:1:66,363] percentage of a project's "qualified basis" an investor in LIHTC projects may deduct from his or her federal income tax liability  

[8:2:66,373] annually in each of ten years. A project's qualified basis is the portion of the total project cost used to calculate the amount of  

[8:3:66,383] the tax credit and typically excludes non-depreciable costs such as the purchase of land. The affordable housing project  

[8:4:66,393] sponsor uses or sells ten times the project's tax-credit allocation amount because investors can take the annual tax credit each  

[8:5:66,404] year for a ten-year period.  

[9:0:66,421] The federal per-capita tax credit ceiling for 9-percent credits is calculated annually and indexed for inflation.   For 2018, each  

[9:1:66,431] state has an annual housing credit ceiling of $2.40 per   state resident.   Additionally, each state may qualify annually for a share  

[9:2:66,442] of unused credits in a national pool.  

[10:0:66,459] Developments financed with tax-exempt bond proceeds may receive the 4% federal tax credit. The sponsors of such projects  

[10:1:66,470] must apply to the Committee and must conform to applicable federal and state statutory and regulatory requirements, but there  

[10:2:66,480] is no annual cap on the amount of credit that may be awarded by the state to such developments.  

[10:3:66,497] Under federal law, credit projects must remain affordable for at least 30 years. However, California's program generally requires  

[10:4:66,508] maintaining affordability for 55 years. Land use agreements are recorded against each credit project to ensure compliance.  

[11:0:66,536] The State LIHTC Program  

[12:0:66,556] In 1987, recognizing the high cost of housing in California, the Legislature authorized the state's program to augment the  

[12:1:66,566] federal program. Housing projects receiving (or that have previously received) an allocation of federal tax credits may apply for  

[12:2:66,576] an allocation of state tax credits. Projects serving farmworkers may apply for state tax credits regardless of their federal tax  

[12:3:66,587] credit status.  

[13:0:66,607] The annual state credit ceiling is indexed for inflation, and for 2018, was $98.6 million. Investors take the state tax credit  

[13:1:66,617] annually over a four-year period in contrast to the ten-year federal period.  

[14:0:66,638] Farmworker Housing Program  

[15:0:66,658] Chapter 521, Statutes of 2008, folded the previous Farmworker Housing Assistance Tax Credit program into the general state  

[15:1:66,668] LIHTC program as a $500,000 annual set-aside in support of farmworker housing. Pursuant to Chapter 372, Statutes of 2017,  

[15:2:66,678] these credits differ from other state credits in that the credit percentage for tax-exempt bond financed projects is higher and  

[15:3:66,689] projects may receive state credits even if they receive an increase in their federal tax credit basis.  

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[1:0:88,43] 0971   California Alternative Energy and Advanced Transportation Financing  

[1:1:279,57] Authority  

[2:0:66,78] The California Alternative Energy and Advanced Transportation Financing Authority was established by Chapter 908, Statutes  

[2:1:66,89] of 1980, to promote the prompt and efficient development of energy sources which are renewable or which more efficiently  

[2:2:66,99] utilize and conserve scarce energy resources. Recognizing the importance of developing a secure energy future to protect the  

[2:3:66,109] environment and ensure economic stability, the Authority advances the state's goals of reducing greenhouse gas emissions by  

[2:4:66,119] providing financing options to assist industries in increasing the deployment of sustainable and renewable energy sources,  

[2:5:66,129] implementing measures that increase the efficiency of the use of energy, creating high quality employment opportunities, and  

[2:6:66,140] lessening the state's dependence on fossil fuels. To support these goals, the Authority provides financing and credit  

[2:7:66,150] enhancements to promote the establishment of facilities that use alternative methods and sources of energy, and facilities  

[2:8:66,160] needed for the development and commercialization of advanced transportation technologies.  

[3:0:66,180] The Authority consists of five members: the State Treasurer, who serves as the chairperson, the State Controller, the Director  

[3:1:66,191] of the Department of Finance, the Chairperson of the State Energy Resources Conservation and Development Commission,  

[3:2:66,201] and the President of the Public Utilities Commission.

[3:0:66,69] Financial assistance can take the form of loans, loan loss reserves, interest rate reductions, proceeds of bonds issued by the  

[3:1:66,79] authority, bond insurance, loan guarantees or other credit enhancements, contributions of money, or a combination thereof, as  

[3:2:66,89] determined and approved by resolution of the Authority.  

[4:0:66,109] In 2010, the Authority launched a sales and use tax exclusion (STE) program for advanced transportation and alternative  

[4:1:66,120] source manufacturing in California (Chapter 10, Statutes of 2010) and subsequently, Chapter 677, Statutes of 2012, expanded  

[4:2:66,130] the STE program to include advanced manufacturing, with an annual cap of $100 million available for STE awards. Chapter  

[4:3:66,140] 768, Statutes of 2015, further expanded the program to also include equipment primarily used to process recycled feedstock  

[4:4:66,150] and equipment that primarily utilizes recycled feedstock in the production of another product. The objective of this program is to  

[4:5:66,160] promote the creation of California-based manufacturing, businesses, and jobs that are aimed at reducing greenhouse gases,  

[4:6:66,171] air and water pollution, and energy consumption.  

[5:0:66,191] Legislation in 2010 (Chapter 15, Statutes of 2010), 2011 (Chapter 9, Statutes of 2011, First Extraordinary Session), and 2013  

[5:1:66,201] (Chapter 356, Statutes of 2013), authorized financial assistance to encourage energy efficiency retrofits. The Authority  

[5:2:66,211] developed a loan loss reserve program to assist financial institutions in making loans to homeowners in the state for residential  

[5:3:66,222] whole house energy efficiency and renewable energy projects, and developed a risk mitigation program for residential Property  

[5:4:66,232] Assessed Clean Energy programs in California.  

[6:0:66,252] Most recently, the Budget Act of 2014 authorized administration of the California Hub for Energy Efficiency Financing on behalf  

[6:1:66,262] of, and in collaboration with, the California Public Utilities Commission. These energy efficiency financing pilot programs will  

[6:2:66,273] employ various types of credit enhancements to encourage and leverage private capital lending (in both the residential and  

[6:3:66,283] commercial sectors) for energy efficiency improvements needed to help achieve California's energy efficiency goals.

[1:0:151,43] 0974   California Pollution Control Financing Authority  

[2:0:66,64] California Pollution Control Financing Authority is committed to stimulating local economies in California by making capital more  

[2:1:66,74] accessible to small businesses, and delivering innovative financing for projects that protect and restore the environment. The  

[2:2:66,84] Authority was created to assist the solid waste, recycling, water, and wastewater industries through its Pollution Control Tax-

[2:3:66,95] Exempt Bond Program. Over the last twenty-five years, the Authority has evolved to provide financing assistance to California's  

[2:4:66,105] small business sector through its California Capital Access Program (CalCAP), and to promote the reuse and redevelopment of  

[2:5:66,115] brownfields through the California Recycle Underutilized Sites Program (CALReUSE).  

[3:0:66,135] The Authority consists of the State Treasurer (Chairperson), the State Controller, and the Director of the Department of  

[3:1:66,146] Finance.  

[4:0:66,172] 3-YEAR EXPENDITURES AND POSITIONS  †

[14:0:66,681] 0860 - POLLUTION CONTROL TAX-EXEMPT BOND PROGRAM  

[15:0:66,701] The objective of this program is to provide bond financing to California businesses, irrespective of company size, for the  

[15:1:66,712] acquisition, construction, or installation of qualified pollution control, waste disposal, water furnishing, wastewater treatment,

# === PAGE 246 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] 2019-20 STATE BUDGET — LJE   244 

[1:0:382,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE 

[2:0:116,32] 0974   California Pollution Control Financing Authority - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] waste recovery facilities, and the acquisition and installation of new equipment. Tax-exempt financing issued by the Authority  

[3:1:66,79] assists municipalities in complying with waste diversion mandates of the California Integrated Waste Management Act of 1989.  

[3:2:66,89] As of June 30, 2018, bonds totaling approximately $15.6 billion have been issued by the Authority.  

[4:0:66,107] 0865 - CALIFORNIA CAPITAL ACCESS PROGRAM FOR SMALL BUSINESSES  

[5:0:66,127] The objective of this program is to encourage banks and other financial institutions to make loans to small businesses. CalCAP  

[5:1:66,137] for Small Businesses is a form of loan loss recovery that may provide up to 100 percent coverage on certain loan defaults. By  

[5:2:66,148] participating in CalCAP, lenders have available to them a proven financing mechanism to meet the financing needs of  

[5:3:66,158] California's small businesses. The program works through the creation of a loan loss-reserve fund for each participating  

[5:4:66,168] financial institution. The Authority funds this reserve together with the financial institution and the borrower. Additional  

[6:0:66,178] incentives are provided to lend to businesses located in specified communities. The reserve serves to reduce loan-loss risk,  

[6:1:66,188] allowing banks to lend to targeted California small businesses. Chapter 731, Statutes of 2010, appropriated $6 million General  

[6:2:66,199] Fund to CalCAP to increase lending efforts. As of June 30, 2018, approximately $750,000 of the $6 million remained in the  

[6:3:66,209] State-funded program account to assist small businesses.  

[7:0:66,229] In addition, California was awarded an allocation of federal funds in the amount of $168.6 million from the federal State Small  

[7:1:66,239] Business Credit Initiative (SSBCI). The Authority and the Governor's Office of Business and Economic Development (Go-BIZ)  

[7:2:66,250] equally share this allocation of $84.3 million each. These funds have enabled the Authority to expand the availability of its  

[7:3:66,260] CalCAP program statewide. The Authority also launched the Collateral Support Program to assist more small businesses and  

[7:4:66,270] utilize the SSBCI federal funds.   As of June 30, 2018,   the federally-funded program account to assist small businesses under  

[7:5:66,280] the CalCAP loan loss reserve program was fully-expended. Approximately $1 million remained in the federally-funded program  

[7:6:66,290] account for the Collateral Support Program, obligated to pre-approved loans. Funds are being recaptured to sustain both  

[7:7:66,301] programs.  

[8:0:66,321] Utilizing the CalCAP model, the Authority has partnered with the Air Resources Board (ARB) to assist diesel truck and  

[8:1:66,331] equipment owners in meeting new clean air requirements by directing a total of $107.3 million in Air Quality Improvement  

[8:2:66,341] Program funds towards the purchase or retrofit of diesel trucks to comply with ARB's Statewide Truck and Bus Rule. The  

[8:3:66,352] Authority has also partnered with the California Energy Commission to implement a $2 million pilot program to provide credit  

[8:4:66,362] enhancements and rebates to small business borrowers who install electric vehicle charging stations. Similarly, the Authority is  

[8:5:66,372] partnering with the Department of Resources, Recycling, and Recovery to assist with the financing of important state recycling  

[8:6:66,382] objectives.  

[9:0:66,400] 0870 - CALIFORNIA RECYCLE UNDERUTILIZED SITES PROGRAM  

[10:0:66,418] The CALReUSE program assists with the reuse and redevelopment of underutilized properties with real or perceived  

[11:0:66,428] contamination issues. CALReUSE addresses a funding and information gap in the development of contaminated properties  

[11:1:66,438] (brownfields) to help bring these properties into productive reuse. Beginning in 2000, the CALReUSE Assessment Program  

[11:2:66,448] provided forgivable loans of up to $300,000, which was later increased to $500,000 per brownfield site. The funds assisted with  

[11:3:66,458] brownfield site assessment and characterization, technical assistance, and the development of remedial action plans. Eligible  

[11:4:66,469] projects included sites with potential beneficial reuse not currently redeveloped due to lack of information about real or  

[11:5:66,479] perceived contamination, uncertainty about clean-up costs, or concerns regarding time frames and the regulatory process.  

[12:0:66,496] Additionally, Proposition 1C, the Housing and Emergency Shelter Trust Fund Act of 2006, included provisions to fund  

[13:0:66,507] brownfield cleanup that resulted in the expansion of the CALReUSE Program. The CALReUSE Remediation Program received  

[13:1:66,517] $60 million in Proposition 1C funds and provided up to $5 million per project in loans and grants for the purpose of brownfield  

[13:2:66,527] cleanup that promotes affordable infill residential and mixed-used development. All CALReUSE Program funds have been  

[13:3:66,537] awarded. The CALReUSE Program's $60 million investment in cleanup of contaminated sites will result in 5,618 housing units  

[13:4:66,547] in 30 California communities.  

[14:0:66,565] 0875 - ALTERNATIVE FINANCING PROGRAMS  

[15:0:66,583] Under its authority to provide alternative methods of financing facilities for pollution control, clean water supply and alternative  

[15:1:66,593] energy production, the Authority is developing alternative financing models to assist sister agencies with achieving the state's  

[15:2:66,603] environmental goals. The Authority is authorized to receive and accept contributions from other sources including federal and  

[15:3:66,613] state agencies to carry out the purposes of its statutory authority.  

[16:0:66,631] 0876 - CALIFORNIA CAPITAL ACCESS PROGRAM FOR COMPLIANCE WITH THE AMERICANS WITH DISABLITIES ACT  

[17:0:66,649] The objective of this program, created by Chapter 787, Statutes of 2015, is to help small businesses comply with the federal  

[17:1:66,659] Americans with Disabilities Act and increase access for their employees and customers by encouraging lenders and other  

[17:2:66,669] financial institutions to make loans to very small businesses to finance tenant improvements. The Legislature provided the  

[17:3:66,679] Authority an appropriation of $10 million effective January 1, 2016, to administer a credit enhancement program following the  

[17:4:66,690] CalCAP model and create loan loss reserve accounts for lenders that enroll qualifying loans into the program.  

[18:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,69] 0877 - CALIFORNIA SEISMIC SAFETY CAPITAL ACCESS LOAN PROGRAM  

[4:0:66,89] The California Seismic Safety Capital Access Loan Program, authorized by Chapter 32, Statutes of 2016, provided a one-time  

[4:1:66,99] allocation of $10 million effective January 1, 2017 to create an accessible loan program to qualified small businesses and  

[4:2:66,109] residential property owners (including multi-unit dwellings and mobile homes registered by the California Department of  

[4:3:66,120] Housing and Community Development) for costs related to seismic retrofitting. The Program encourages banks and other  

[4:4:66,130] financial institutions to participate by creating loan loss reserve accounts for lenders that enroll qualifying loans into the  

[4:5:66,140] program. The loans to small businesses and residential property owners are for financing seismic retrofits of real property to  

[4:6:66,150] reduce losses and mitigate seismic damage.

[1:0:154,43] 0977   California Health Facilities Financing Authority  

[2:0:66,64] The mission of the California Health Facilities Financing Authority is to help eligible and credit worthy nonprofit and public  

[2:1:66,74] health facilities reduce their cost of capital, and promote health care improvement and cost containment objectives by providing  

[2:2:66,84] cost-effective tax-exempt bond, low-cost loan, and direct grant programs.  

[3:0:66,102] The Authority was established by Chapter 1033, Statutes of 1979 (AB 1558), and consists of nine members: the State  

[3:1:66,112] Treasurer, the Director of the Department of Finance, the State Controller, two public members appointed by the Senate, two  

[3:2:66,123] public members appointed by the Assembly, and two public members appointed by the Governor.

[4:0:66,239] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:1:66,257] 0880 - CHILDREN'S HOSPITAL PROGRAM  

[5:0:66,275] In 2004, California voters approved Proposition 61, which established the Children's Hospital Program. In 2008, Proposition 3  

[5:1:66,285] established the second Children's Hospital Program. In 2018, Proposition 4 established a third Children’s Hospital Program.  

[5:2:66,296] The purpose of the three programs is to improve the health and welfare of California's critically ill children by providing a stable  

[5:3:66,306] and ready source of funds for capital improvement projects for children's hospitals. Children's Hospital Program grant funding is  

[5:4:66,316] derived from the issuance of general obligation bonds, up to $750 million under Proposition 61, $980 million under Proposition  

[5:5:66,326] 3, and $1.5 billion under Proposition 4.  

[5:6:66,344] 0885 - HEALTH FACILITIES GRANTS AND LOANS  

[6:0:66,364] The Authority serves as a conduit provider of tax-exempt bonds and a direct provider of financial assistance to health  

[6:1:66,374] institutions.  

[7:0:66,395] Tax-Exempt Bond Program  

[8:0:66,415] Bonds issued under this conduit program are not a debt, liability, or a pledge of the full faith and credit of the taxing power of  

[8:1:66,425] the state or any of its political subdivisions. The full faith and credit of the participating institutions are pledged for repayment of  

[8:2:66,436] the bonds. To qualify for funding, the proposed project must be a health facility, operated by a private nonprofit corporation or  

[8:3:66,446] association, city, city and county, county, or hospital district.  

[9:0:66,466] Lifeline Grant Program  

[10:0:66,487] Chapter 52, Statutes of 2017 (SB 97) authorized the Authority to approve grants of up to $20 million dollars from the HELP II  

[10:1:66,497] Loan Program subfund account. The Lifeline Grant Program assists small and rural health facilities, including community-based  

[10:2:66,507] clinics, that may be adversely affected financially by a reduction or elimination of federal government assistance and that have  

[10:3:66,517] little to no access to working capital. Grants must be awarded by June 30, 2020.  

[11:0:66,538] HELP II Loan Program  

[12:0:66,558] The Authority administers the Healthcare Expansion Loan Program II (HELP II) to assist small and rural health facilities in  

[12:1:66,568] obtaining financing for their capital needs. The HELP II Program provides two percent and three percent fixed interest rate  

[12:2:66,578] loans of up to $1,500,000 to California's nonprofit small and rural health facilities in an efficient, timely, and cost effective  

[12:3:66,589] manner. HELP II loans may be used to purchase or construct new facilities, remodel or renovate existing facilities, purchase  

[12:4:66,599] equipment and/or furnishings, and refinance existing debt.  

[13:0:66,619] California Health Access Model Program  

[14:0:66,640] Chapter 23, Statutes of 2012 (AB 1467) authorized the California Health Access Model Program (CHAMP), a grant program  

[14:1:66,650] intended to support innovative methods of delivering health care services and improve health outcomes for vulnerable  

[14:2:66,660] populations and communities by bringing services to individuals where they live or congregate.  

[14:3:66,678] 0890 - MENTAL HEALTH WELLNESS GRANTS  

[15:0:66,698] Chapter 34, Statutes of 2013 (SB 82), the Investment in Mental Health Wellness Act of 2013 and related legislation provided  

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[2:0:119,32] 0977   California Health Facilities Financing Authority - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] $142.5 million in one-time General Fund, and $4 million in ongoing Mental Health Services Act funding to provide grants for  

[3:1:66,79] community based mental health crisis support, which may also be eligible for matching federal funding.  

[3:2:66,97] The Act established a grant program to disburse funds to California counties or to their nonprofit or public agency designates  

[3:3:66,107] for the purpose of developing mental health crisis support programs. Specifically, funds will increase capacity for client  

[3:4:66,117] assistance and services in crisis intervention, crisis stabilization, crisis residential treatment, rehabilitative mental health  

[3:5:66,127] services, and mobile crisis support teams. The grants will support capital improvement, expansion and limited start-up costs.  

[4:0:66,148] Investment in Mental Health Wellness Grant Program for Children and Youth  

[5:0:66,165] With the passage of Chapter 30, Statutes of 2016 (SB 833), the Investment in Mental Health Grant Program for Children and  

[5:1:66,175] Youth was created to increase mental health services for children and youth 21 years of age and under to develop a complete  

[5:2:66,186] continuum of crisis services. Working with counties, the program funds facility acquisition, construction/renovation, equipment  

[5:3:66,196] acquisition, and applicable startup or expansion costs to provide mental health services for children and youth as well as  

[5:4:66,206] provide family respite care throughout the state.  

[6:0:66,226] Community Services Infrastructure Grants 

[7:0:66,244] Chapter 33, Statutes of 2016 (SB 843) created the Community Services Infrastructure competitive grant program to expand  

[7:1:66,254] community alternatives to jail and prison. The program seeks to expand access to jail and prison diversion programs and  

[7:2:66,265] services for those with mental health illness, substance use disorders, or who have suffered from trauma. Working with  

[7:3:66,275] counties, the program will fund facility acquisition, renovation, equipment acquisition, and applicable startup or expansion costs  

[7:4:66,285] for facilities that provide services to this population.  

[7:5:66,303] No Place Like Home Program  

[8:0:66,320] Chapter 43, Statutes of 2016 (AB 1618) established the No Place Like Home Program (NPLH), which requires the Housing and  

[8:1:66,331] Community Development Agency (HCD) to award up to $2 billion among counties to fund the acquisition, design, construction,  

[8:2:66,341] rehabilitation, or preservation of permanent supportive housing for individuals living with a severe mental illness who are  

[8:3:66,351] homeless or at risk of chronic homelessness. Chapter 322, Statutes of 2016 (AB 1628) authorized CHFFA to enter into  

[8:4:66,361] contracts with HCD and further authorized CHFFA to issue up to $2 billion in taxable revenue bonds pursuant to the NPLH  

[8:5:66,371] Program.

[1:0:211,43] 0981   California ABLE Act Board  

[2:0:66,64] The California Achieving a Better Life Experience Act (ABLE) Board was established by Chapter 796, Statutes of 2015 (SB  

[2:1:66,74] 324) to create a Qualified ABLE Program. The Program will provide eligible individuals with disabilities the opportunity to save  

[2:2:66,84] private funds in tax-advantaged ABLE accounts for the purpose of supporting persons with disabilities to maintain their health,  

[2:3:66,95] independence, and quality of life.

[12:0:66,621] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[12:1:66,640] 0895 - CALIFORNIA ABLE ACT BOARD  

[13:0:66,660] On December 19, 2014, President Obama signed the Stephen Beck Jr., Achieving a Better Life Experience Act of 2014, which  

[13:1:66,670] allows individuals who became blind or disabled before reaching age 26, to create tax-free savings accounts. Individuals can  

[13:2:66,680] make nondeductible cash contributions to an ABLE account in the name of a designated beneficiary with tax-free earnings.  

[13:3:66,691] ABLE account distributions are also not included in the beneficiary's income, as long as they are used for qualified disability  

[13:4:66,701] expenses. Chapter 774, Statutes of 2015 (AB 449), implements the ABLE Act in California, and directs the Board, with the  

[13:5:66,711] State Treasurer as Chair, to administer the California ABLE Program accounts on behalf of eligible individuals.

[1:0:100,43] 0983   California Urban Waterfront Area Restoration Financing Authority  

[1:1:66,64] Created in 1983, the California Urban Waterfront Area Restoration Financing Authority was established to restore, revitalize  

[1:2:66,74] and develop in an environmentally and economically sound manner, the coastal and inland urban waterfront areas of the state,  

[1:3:66,84] in cooperation with local governments. The Authority consists of five members: the State Treasurer (Chairperson), the Director  

[1:4:66,95] of the Department of Finance, the State Controller, the Secretary of the Natural Resources Agency, and the Executive Director  

[1:5:66,105] of the State Coastal Conservancy.  

[2:0:66,132] 3-YEAR EXPENDITURES AND POSITIONS  †
