[3:3:122,187] Financing Program  - - - $- $- $-  

[3:4:75,205] TOTALS, POSITIONS AND EXPENDITURES (All Programs) - - - $- $- $-  

[4:0:66,242] †   This budget display is for informational purposes only. Public Resource Code section 32054 authorizes an Executive Director;  

[4:1:66,256] however, the position is currently vacant.  

[5:0:66,283] LEGAL CITATIONS AND AUTHORITY  

[5:1:66,301] DEPARTMENT AUTHORITY  

[6:0:66,321] Public Resources Code, Division 22, Sections 32000-32208.  

[7:0:66,358] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[8:0:66,377] 0900 - The Authority was established to issue up to $650 million in conduit financing to make loans or acquire title to property  

[8:1:66,387] and to underwrite or undertake directly a variety of urban waterfront development projects within the coastal zone, the  

[8:2:66,397] Sacramento-Yolo Port District, the Stockton Port District, and those metropolitan statistical areas meeting specified conditions.  

[8:3:66,407] The Federal Tax Reform Act of 1986 requires that bonds authorized by the Authority generally be within an allocation from the  

[8:4:66,417] state's ''private activity'' bond limit in order for the bonds to be federally tax-exempt, unless the issuer qualifies as a private,  

[8:5:66,428] nonprofit business.  

[9:0:66,448] Financing is available for both publicly and privately sponsored projects that provide visitor-serving facilities, waterfront-

[9:1:66,458] dependent industries, public recreation, and erosion control facilities. The State Coastal Conservancy must approve both the  

[9:2:66,468] specific project and a master plan for urban waterfront restoration before any project can obtain the Authority approval for  

[9:3:66,479] revenue bond financing. The Authority has sold $3.33 million in revenue bonds to date.

[1:0:106,43] 0984   California Secure Choice Retirement Savings Investment Board  

[2:0:66,64] The California Secure Choice Retirement Savings Investment Board was established by Chapter 734, Statutes of 2012 (SB  

[2:1:66,74] 1234). Subsequently, Chapter 804, Statutes of 2016 (SB 1234), authorized the Board to implement the CalSavers Retirement  

[2:2:66,84] Savings Program (Program), which is a state-administered retirement savings program for private sector employees in  

[2:3:66,95] California with no access to workplace retirement savings plans.  

[3:0:66,112] The Board consists of nine members: the State Treasurer (Chairperson), the Director of the Department of Finance, the State  

[3:1:66,123] Controller, a retirement savings and investment expert appointed by the Senate Committee on Rules, an employee  

[3:2:66,133] representative appointed by the Speaker of the Assembly, a small business representative appointed by the Governor, a public  

[3:3:66,143] member appointed by the Governor, and two additional members appointed by the Governor.

[11:0:66,601] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[11:1:66,619] 0910 - CALSAVERS  

[12:0:66,637] The Program provides employees a retirement savings program without the administrative complexity, fees, or fiduciary liability  

[12:1:66,647] of existing options for employers. Any employer with at least five employees that does not already offer a workplace retirement  

[12:2:66,658] savings vehicle will be required to either begin offering one via the private market or provide their employees with access to the  

[12:3:66,668] Program. A pilot version of the Program was launched in November 2018, which runs until June 2019. The Program is fully  

[12:4:66,678] launching on July 1, 2019.

[1:0:185,43] 0985   California School Finance Authority  

[2:0:66,64] The California School Finance Authority (CSFA), created in 1985, provides facilities and working capital financing to school  

[2:1:66,74] districts, community college districts, county offices of education, and charter schools. The State Treasurer serves as chair of  

[2:2:66,84] CSFA and the Superintendent of Public Instruction and the Director of Finance serve as members. CSFA has offices in Los  

[2:3:66,95] Angeles and Sacramento.  

[3:0:66,115] CSFA serves as the primary state agency for California charter schools seeking facility and working capital assistance by  

[3:1:66,125] providing access to low-cost financing through several State and federally funded programs.

[2:0:150,32] 0985   California School Finance Authority - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,87] 0918 - SMART BONDS PROGRAM  

[4:0:66,107] Chapter 1438, Statutes of 1985, as amended by Chapter 598, Statutes of 1987, established CSFA and authorized the issuance  

[4:1:66,118] of revenue bonds or other debt instruments. The proceeds from the sale of the bonds were available for loans to schools and  

[4:2:66,128] community college districts to assist with the acquisition of equipment and new school sites, construction of new facilities,  

[4:3:66,138] reconstruction of existing facilities, capital improvements, and to provide working capital. Chapter 325, Statutes of 2006 (AB  

[4:4:66,148] 2717), allows CSFA to issue debt on behalf of California charter schools for capital improvements and working capital needs.  

[4:5:66,166] 0920 - CHARTER SCHOOL FACILITIES PROGRAM  

[5:0:66,186] Chapter 935, Statutes of 2002, as amended by Chapter 587, Statutes of 2003, created the Charter School Facilities Program  

[5:1:66,196] (CSFP), which provides funding for the new construction, renovation or rehabilitation of charter school facilities. CSFA and the  

[5:2:66,207] Office of Public School Construction jointly administer the program. CSFP was funded through the Kindergarten-University  

[5:3:66,217] Public Education Facilities Bond Acts of 2002, 2004, 2006, and 2016, for a total of $1.4 billion. The program provides a 50  

[5:4:66,227] percent state subsidy for the charter school facilities project costs, with the balance of the project costs being repaid (to the  

[5:5:66,237] state) by the charter school in the form of a long-term lease. Recipient charter schools must provide site-based instruction, be  

[5:6:66,247] deemed financially sound by CSFA, and meet other program eligibility requirements.  

[5:7:66,265] 0925 - STATE CHARTER SCHOOL FACILITIES INCENTIVE GRANTS PROGRAM  

[6:0:66,286] In 2004, 2009, and 2014, CSFA was awarded grants under the United States Department of Education's State Charter School  

[6:1:66,296] Facilities Incentive Grants Program (CFDA 84.282D) to provide California charter schools with assistance for facilities costs.  

[6:2:66,306] Grant funds reimburse a charter school's costs for rent, lease, mortgage or debt service payments for existing or new facilities  

[6:3:66,316] or the costs of acquiring land and/or constructing or renovating a facility. Grants are awarded to charter schools based on  

[6:4:66,326] preference points allotted by the percentage of low-income students, percentage of overcrowding, not-for-profit status, and  

[6:5:66,337] demonstrated student performance. Schools cannot use program funds to supplant state funding.  

[6:6:66,354] 0930 - CHARTER SCHOOL FACILITY GRANT PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,375] The Charter School Facility Grant Program provides Proposition 98 General Fund grants to assist charter schools with rent and  

[7:1:66,385] lease costs. This program targets schools and communities with significant populations of economically disadvantaged  

[7:2:66,395] students. Eligible charter schools are provided up to $1,187 per unit of eligible average daily attendance, not to exceed 75  

[7:3:66,405] percent of their total annual facilities rent or lease costs.  

[7:4:66,423] 0935 - CHARTER SCHOOL REVOLVING LOAN FUND  

[8:0:66,443] Charter 1010, Statutes of 1976 established the Charter School Revolving Loan Fund in the State Treasury to provide loans of  

[8:1:66,454] up to $250,000 to new charter schools to assist them in meeting the purposes of the school's approved charter. The program is  

[8:2:66,464] available to any charter school that is not a conversion of an existing public school, and preference is given to schools that  

[8:3:66,474] have not completed their full charter term.

[0:0:66,13] LEGISLATIVE, JUDICIAL, AND EXECUTIVE   2019-20 STATE BUDGET — LJE   269 

[1:0:168,43] 0989   California Educational Facilities Authority  

[2:0:66,64] The California Educational Facilities Authority (CEFA) provides qualified nonprofit higher education institutions with assistance  

[2:1:66,74] through a tax-exempt revenue bond program to reduce the costs of financing academic facilities.   CEFA may also issue bonds,  

[2:2:66,84] notes, and other forms of indebtedness for student loans to support students' costs of higher education.  

[3:0:66,105] CEFA consists of the following five members: the Director of Finance, the State Controller, the State Treasurer, and two public  

[3:1:66,115] members appointed by the Governor.  

[4:0:66,145] 3-YEAR EXPENDITURES AND POSITIONS

[12:0:66,576] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[12:1:66,595] 0940 - BOND FINANCING  

[13:0:66,612] CEFA issues tax-exempt revenue bonds to assist private educational institutions of higher learning to construct educational  

[13:1:66,622] facilities.   Because it is authorized to issue tax-exempt bonds,   CEFA may be able to provide more favorable financing terms  

[13:2:66,633] than might otherwise be obtainable.   CEFA also may include qualifying nonprofit entities as eligible program participants for the  

[13:3:66,643] construction of student and faculty housing.   Bonds issued by CEFA are not a debt, liability, or claim on the faith and credit or  

[13:4:66,653] the taxing power of the State of California or any of its political subdivisions.   The full faith and credit of the participating  

[13:5:66,663] institution is normally pledged to the payment of the bonds.   Bonds issued for this purpose are not subject to the state's "private  

[13:6:66,673] activity" bond ceiling as specified in federal law.  

[14:0:66,691] For purposes of the California Educational Facilities Act, "private college" or "private participating college" means a private  

[14:1:66,701] college that does not restrict the admission of a student based on his or her race or ethnicity, provided that the financing does  

[14:2:66,712] not violate constitutional provisions.  

[15:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[2:0:133,32] 0989   California Educational Facilities Authority - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] "Bond" means bonds, notes, debentures, securities, or other evidences of indebtedness.   This broad definition allows CEFA to  

[3:1:66,79] issue tax-exempt direct or private placement loans for colleges and universities, which may provide greater cost savings than  

[3:2:66,89] these colleges and universities might otherwise realize on a traditional bond financing.  

[4:0:66,109] 0955 - COLLEGE ACCESS TAX CREDIT FUND  

[5:0:66,129] Chapter 367, Statutes of 2014, required CEFA to administer the College Access Tax Credit Fund and allocate and certify the  

[5:1:66,139] tax credits for taxable years beginning on or after January 1, 2014, and before January 1, 2017.   Chapter 22, Statutes of 2015,  

[5:2:66,150] added a requirement that CEFA continue to allocate and certify the tax credits for taxable years beginning on or after January  

[5:3:66,160] 1, 2017, and before January 1, 2018.   Chapter 527, Statutes of 2017, extended CEFA's responsibility to administer the tax  

[5:4:66,170] credits for taxable years beginning on or after January 1, 2017, and before January 1, 2023.
